porcius vvhen feſtus come province thre dayes aſcended frō ceſarea vnto ieruſalem enformed hye preſtes chefe iewes paul ſought deſired faveour agaynſt wold ſende ieruſalem layde awayte waye kill daye ſate doune iudgemēt ſeate commaunded paul brought come iewes come frō ieruſalem came aboute layde many greveous complayntes agaynſt paul coulde prove longe anſwered ſelfe nether agaynſt lawe iewes nether agaynſt temple yet agaynſt ceſar offended eny thinge feſtus willinge iewes pleaſure anſwered paul ſayde wilt thou goo ieruſalem iudged theſe thinges ſayd paul ſtonde ceſars iudgemēt eye art ware beame thyn awne eye though thou kepe lawe outewardly workes feare rebuke ſhame punyſſhement loue rewarde vauntage and▪ vayne glory yet doeſt thou luſt loue towarde lawe haddeſt leuer greate deale wyſe yf thou dydeſt feare lawe▪ ye inwardly thyne herte thou woldeſt ther lawe yet god auctor vengear lawe yf poſſible ſo paynefull vnto thyne appetytes refrayned kepte doune wherfore playne concluſion thou grounde botome thyne herte arte ennymye lawe prevayſeth nowe thou teacheſt man ſteale hen thou thyne awne ſelfe arte thefe thyne hert outwardly woldeſt fayne ſteale yf thou durſt though outwarde dedes abyde alwaye behynde ſoch ypocrites diſſimulars breake forth amonge euen euyll ſcabbe pocke wayes kepte violence medicine thou teacheſt man teacheſt thy ſelfe ye thou woteſt thou teacheſt thou vnderſtondeſt lawe ryght cannot fulfylled ſatiſfyed vnfayned loue affecyon ſo greately fulfylled outeward dedes workes moreouer lawe encreaſeth ſynne ſayth fyfte chapter frewill awne proper ſtrengthe enforſynge withſtondynge though neuyr ſo greate workynge yet longe ther remayneth herte vnluſt tediouſnes grudgyng grief payne lothſumnes compulſion toward lawe ſo longe workes vnprofitable loſt ye damnable ſighte god meaneth paul thryde chapter ſayeth dedes y• lawe ſhall fleſſhe iuſtified ſyghte god perceaueſt thou thoſe ſophiſters diſceauers whiche teache man maye
